# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Hot Restart Mechanism

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the hot restart mechanism: the HotRestart interface, the parent/child process handshake, the socket passing via Unix domain sockets, the drain sequence, and the child process readiness signaling.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

68-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Envoy hot restart mechanism and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The answer includes **14 C++ source files** that implement the hot restart mechanism across the following components:

**Core Architecture:**
- **HotRestart Interface** - Defines the abstraction for live process restart
- **HotRestartImpl** - Main Linux implementation managing shared memory, process coordination
- **HotRestartingParent** - Handles parent process socket/stats/drain requests
- **HotRestartingChild** - Handles child process initialization and parent communication
- **HotRestartingBase + RpcStream** - Low-level Unix domain socket communication

**Key Mechanisms Covered:**
1. **Parent/Child Handshake** - Via Unix domain sockets (AF_UNIX, SOCK_DGRAM)
2. **Socket Passing** - Using SCM_RIGHTS ancillary data in sendmsg()
3. **Drain Sequence** - Parent gracefully closes listeners and forwards unmatched QUIC packets to child
4. **Child Readiness** - Signaled through drainParentListeners() and shared memory initialization flags
5. **Shared Memory** - Process-shared pthread mutexes and version checking
6. **Stats Merging** - Parent exports gauges and counter deltas to child
7. **UDP Forwarding** - Separate RPC stream for QUIC packet routing during drain

The implementation uses Protocol Buffers for message serialization and supports up to 3 concurrent Envoy processes for hot restart.

interruption. The implementation involves the following key components:\\n\\n## HotRestart Interface (envoy/server/hot_restart.h)\\nDefines the abstract HotRestart interface with methods for:\\n- `drainParentListeners()`: Shutdown parent listeners to begin graceful draining\\n- `duplicateParentListenSocket()`: Retrieve listening sockets from parent process via Unix domain socket file descriptor passing\\n- `registerUdpForwardingListener()`: Register UDP listeners for QUIC packet forwarding from parent to child\\n- `parentDrainedCallbackRegistrar()`: Get interface for registering callbacks when parent is drained\\n- `sendParentAdminShutdownRequest()`: Request parent to shutdown admin functionality\\n- `sendParentTerminateRequest()`: Signal parent process to terminate\\n- `mergeParentStatsIfAny()`: Merge parent statistics into child's stats store\\n- `initialize()`: Initialize parent/child logic after startup\\n\\n## HotRestartImpl (source/server/hot_restart_impl.h, .cc)\\nThe main Linux implementation that:\\n- Creates or attaches to a shared memory segment (named via `/envoy_shared_memory_{base_id}`) containing `SharedMemory` struct\\n- Initializes process-shared pthread mutexes (`ProcessSharedMutex`) for logging and access log synchronization\\n- Manages both parent and child aspects via `HotRestartingParent` and `HotRestartingChild` instances\\n- Calls `attachSharedMemory()` to manage shared memory lifecycle with version checking (HOT_RESTART_VERSION)\\n- Sets `PR_SET_PDEATHSIG` to ensure child terminates if parent dies unexpectedly\\n- Delegates to child/parent for actual handshake and socket passing\\n\\n## Shared Memory and Synchronization\\nThe `SharedMemory` struct stores:\\n- `size_` and `version_`: For compatibility checking between processes\\n- `log_lock_` and `access_log_lock_`: Process-shared pthread mutexes\\n- `flags_`: Atomic flags including `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` to prevent simultaneous initialization\\n\\n## Parent/Child Handshake (HotRestartingBase)\\nBoth parent and child inherit from `HotRestartingBase` which provides:\\n- `RpcStream` class: Manages Unix domain socket communication using SOCK_DGRAM (datagram mode) for atomic message delivery\\n- Socket binding via `bindDomainSocket()` with naming scheme: `{socket_path}_{role}_{base_id}`\\n- Two separate RPC streams: main stream for control messages, UDP forwarding stream for QUIC packet forwarding\\n- Protocol: Length-prefixed protobuf messages sent via `sendmsg()` with ancillary data for file descriptor passing (CMSG_RIGHTS)\\n\\n## Parent Process (HotRestartingParent in source/server/hot_restarting_parent.h, .cc)\\nHandles requests from child:\\n- Creates two domain sockets: one for main RPC, one for UDP forwarding\\n- `initialize()`: Registers socket event handler on dispatcher for receiving child requests\\n- `onSocketEvent()`: Processes incoming `HotRestartMessage::Request` from child\\n- Request handling via `Internal` class:\\n  - `getListenSocketsForChild()`: Looks up listener by address, extracts listening socket fd, passes via SCM_RIGHTS\\n  - `exportStatsToChild()`: Exports gauges and counters with latched values and dynamic span information\\n  - `drainListeners()`: Initiates graceful drain with UDP packet handler for forwarding undeliverable QUIC packets\\n  - `shutdownAdmin()`: Shuts down parent's admin interface so child can take over\\n- Increments `hot_restart_generation` gauge for tracking generations\\n\\n## Child Process (HotRestartingChild in source/server/hot_restarting_child.h, .cc)\\nRequests from parent and manages readiness:\\n- Creates domain sockets with addresses derived from restart_epoch (0 = first process, 1 = second, etc., cycling mod 3)\\n- `initialize()`: Optionally tests connection to parent; if no parent and `skip_hot_restart_on_no_parent` is set, proceeds as standalone\\n- `duplicateParentListenSocket()`: Sends request message, blocks receiving response with file descriptor\\n- `drainParentListeners()`: Sends drain request (no reply expected), marks child ready to receive traffic\\n- `getParentStats()`: Sends stats request, receives protobuf with gauge values, counter deltas, and dynamic spans\\n- `mergeParentStats()`: Creates `StatMerger` to merge parent stats while handling scope-based temporaries\\n- `sendParentAdminShutdownRequest()`: Requests parent shutdown admin, receives original start time\\n- `sendParentTerminateRequest()`: Signals parent to terminate, cleans up stat merger\\n- `registerParentDrainedCallback()`: Registers callbacks for UDP listeners that wait for parent drain\\n- `onSocketEventUdpForwarding()`: Receives forwarded QUIC UDP packets from parent during drain\\n- `UdpForwardingContext`: Maps listener addresses to listener configs for packet routing\\n\\n## Protocol Buffers (source/server/hot_restart.proto)\\nDefines `HotRestartMessage` with:\\n- Request types: `PassListenSocket`, `ShutdownAdmin`, `Stats`, `DrainListeners`, `Terminate`, `ForwardedUdpPacket`, `TestConnection`\\n- Reply types: `PassListenSocket` (with fd via control message), `ShutdownAdmin`, `Stats` (with gauges, counter deltas, dynamics)\\n- Embedded message structures for multi-chunk protobuf transmission (up to 4096 bytes per datagram)\\n\\n## OS System Calls (envoy/api/os_sys_calls_hot_restart.h)\\nAbstract interface for hot restart specific system calls:\\n- `shmOpen()`: Wrapper around `shm_open()` for creating/opening shared memory\\n- `shmUnlink()`: Wrapper for `shm_unlink()` to remove shared memory objects\\n\\n## Implementation (source/common/api/posix/os_sys_calls_impl_hot_restart.cc)\\nPOSIX implementation with `HotRestartOsSysCallsSingleton` for single-threaded access.\\n\\n## Drain Sequence\\n1. Child calls `drainParentListeners()` after initialization completes\\n2. Parent receives `DrainListeners` request and calls `server_->drainListeners()` with `NonDispatchedUdpPacketHandler`\\n3. Parent begins closing listeners and draining existing connections\\n4. Child registers UDP forwarding listeners via `registerUdpForwardingListener()`\\n5. UDP packets not matching parent connections are forwarded to child via UDP forwarding RPC stream\\n6. Child's `onSocketEventUdpForwarding()` routes packets to appropriate worker via `listenerWorkerRouter`\\n7. After drain timeout, parent terminates\\n\\n## Child Readiness Signaling\\nChild readiness is signaled through:\\n- `drainParentListeners()` call indicates child is ready to receive new traffic\\n- Shared memory `flags_` with `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` cleared once child is fully initialized\\n- Parent drain completion triggers registered callbacks via `registerParentDrainedCallback()`\\n- Generation counter increment in shared memory tracks successive hot restarts\\n\\nThis architecture enables zero-downtime updates by coordinating socket handoff, stats merging, and graceful listener drain between parent and child processes using Unix domain sockets and shared memory primitives.\"\n}\n",

After drain timeout, parent terminates\\n\\n## Child Readiness Signaling\\nChild readiness is signaled through:\\n- `drainParentListeners()` call indicates child is ready to receive new traffic\\n- Shared memory `flags_` with `SHMEM_FLAGS_INITIALIZING` cleared once child is fully initialized\\n- Parent drain completion triggers registered callbacks via `registerParentDrainedCallback()`\\n- Generation counter increment in shared memory tracks successive hot restarts\\n\\nThis architecture enables zero-downtime updates by coordinating socket handoff, stats merging, and graceful listener drain between parent and child processes using Unix domain sockets and shared memory primitives.\"\n}\n",
